plates of the Republic of Ireland">Vehicle index<br />mark code</a></th><td class="infobox-data">D</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>County Dublin</b> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">Contae Bhaile \xc3\x81tha Cliath</i><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> or <i>Contae \xc3\x81tha Cliath</i>) is one of the <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Ireland" title="Counties of Ireland">thirty-two traditional counties of Ireland</a>. Prior to 1994 it was also an administrative county covering the whole county outside of <a href="/wiki/Dublin_City_Council" title="Dublin City Council">Dublin City Council</a>. In 1994, as part of a reorganisation of local government within Dublin the boundaries of Dublin City were redrawn, Dublin County Council was abolished and three new administrative county councils were established: <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire%E2%80%93Rathdown" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fingal" title="Fingal">Fingal</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Dublin" title="South Dublin">South Dublin</a>. \n</p><p>While it is no longer used as an administrative division for local government, it retains a strong identity in popular culture. There still exists a <a href="/wiki/Sheriff#Republic_of_Ireland" title="Sheriff">sheriff</a> appointed for County Dublin.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Constituency_Commission" title="Constituency Commission">Constituency Commissions</a> are must avoid breaching county boundaries when delineating <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_constituencies" title="D\xc3\xa1il constituencies">D\xc3\xa1il constituencies</a>, the three new counties in Dublin are excepted.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It is in the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ireland" title="Provinces of Ireland">province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Leinster" title="Leinster">Leinster</a>, and is named after the city of <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> of Ireland. County Dublin was one of the first parts of Ireland to be <a href="/wiki/Shire" title="Shire">shired</a> by <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">John, King of England</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Norman_invasion_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman invasion of Ireland">Norman invasion of Ireland</a>. \n</p><p>According to the 2016 census, the total population of County Dublin was 1,345,402, approximately 27% of the Republic of Ireland\'s population.<sup id="cite_ref-census2016_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2016-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The county is a <a href="/wiki/NUTS_3_statistical_regions_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="NUTS 3 statistical regions of the Republic of Ireland">NUTS 3</a> region,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and is part of the NUTS 2 region of Eastern and Midland.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government_and_politics">Local government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Local government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_authorities">Local authorities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Local authorities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are four <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">local authorities</a> whose remit collectively encompasses the geographic area of the county and city of Dublin. These are <a href="/wiki/Dublin_City_Council" title="Dublin City Council">Dublin City Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Dublin_County_Council" title="South Dublin County Council">South Dublin County Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire%E2%80%93Rathdown_County_Council" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown County Council">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown County Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fingal_County_Council" title="Fingal County Council">Fingal County Council</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Dublin_Region2.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Map_of_the_Dublin_Region2.PNG/200px-Map_of_the_Dublin_Region2.PNG" decoding="async" width="200" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8b/Map_of_the_Dublin_Region2.PNG 1.5x" data-file-width="295" data-file-height="413" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Dublin_Region2.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dublin region: 1. <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin City</a>; 2. <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire%E2%80%93Rathdown" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown</a>; 3. <a href="/wiki/Fingal" title="Fingal">Fingal</a>; 4. <a href="/wiki/South_Dublin" title="South Dublin">South Dublin</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_Oireachtas" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of the Oireachtas">enactment</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_(Dublin)_Act_1993" title="Local Government (Dublin) Act 1993">Local Government (Dublin) Act 1993</a>, the county was a unified whole even though it was administered by two local authorities \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Dublin_County_Council" title="Dublin County Council">Dublin County Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Corporation" title="Dublin Corporation">Dublin Corporation</a>. Since the enactment of the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_2001" title="Local Government Act 2001">Local Government Act 2001</a> in particular, the geographic area of the county has been divided between three entities at the level of "county" and a further entity at the level of "city". They rank equally as first level local administrative units of the <a href="/wiki/NUTS_3_statistical_regions_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="NUTS 3 statistical regions of the Republic of Ireland">NUTS 3</a> Dublin Region for <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> purposes. There are 34 <a href="/wiki/NUTS_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland#Local_administrative_units" class="mw-redirect" title="NUTS of the Republic of Ireland">LAU 1</a> entities in the Republic of Ireland. Each <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Local government in the Republic of Ireland">local authority</a> is responsible for certain local <a href="/wiki/Public_services" class="mw-redirect" title="Public services">services</a> such as sanitation, planning and development, libraries, the collection of motor taxation, local roads and <a href="/wiki/Social_housing" class="mw-redirect" title="Social housing">social housing</a>.\n</p><p>Dublin County Council (which did not include the <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> of Dublin) was abolished in 1994 and the area divided among the administrative counties of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire%E2%80%93Rathdown" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fingal" title="Fingal">Fingal</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Dublin" title="South Dublin">South Dublin</a> each with its <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county seat</a>. To these areas may be added the area of Dublin city which collectively comprise the Dublin Region<sup id="cite_ref-r1_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> (<i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">R\xc3\xa9igi\xc3\xbain \xc3\x81tha Cliath</i></i>) and come under the remit of the Dublin Regional Authority.\n</p><p>The area lost its administrative county status in 1994, with Section 9 Part 1(a) of the <i>Local Government (Dublin) Act, 1993</i> stating that "the county shall cease to exist."<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In discussing the legislation to dissolve Dublin County Council, <a href="/wiki/Avril_Doyle" title="Avril Doyle">Avril Doyle</a> <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">TD</a> said, "The Bill before us today effectively abolishes County Dublin, and as one born and bred in these parts of Ireland I find it rather strange that we in this House are abolishing County Dublin. I am not sure whether Dubliners realise that that is what we are about today, but in effect that is the case."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The county is part of the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Dublin (European Parliament constituency)">Dublin</a> constituency for the purposes of <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections in the European Union">European elections</a>. For elections to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a>, the area of the county is currently (2016) divided into eleven constituencies: <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Bay_North_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin Bay North (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin Bay North</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Bay_South_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin Bay South (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin Bay South</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Central_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin Central (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Fingal_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin Fingal (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin Fingal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Mid-West_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin Mid-West (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin Mid-West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_North-West_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin North-West (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin North-West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Rathdown_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin Rathdown (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin Rathdown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_South-Central_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin South-Central (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin South-Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_South-West_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin South-West (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin South-West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_West_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin West (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin West</a>, and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire</a>. Together they return 45 deputies (<a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">TDs</a>) to the D\xc3\xa1il.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Three_Rock_Mountain_Southern_Tor.jpg/220px-Three_Rock_Mountain_Southern_Tor.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Three_Rock_Mountain_Southern_Tor.jpg/330px-Three_Rock_Mountain_Southern_Tor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Three_Rock_Mountain_Southern_Tor.jpg/440px-Three_Rock_Mountain_Southern_Tor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2412" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_Rock_Mountain_Southern_Tor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Three_Rock" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Rock">Three Rock</a> Mountain, Dublin, Ireland looking towards Bray Head</div></div></div>\n<p>Despite the legal status of the Dublin Region, the term "County Dublin" is still in common usage. Many organisations and sporting teams continue to organise on a "County Dublin" or "Dublin Region" basis. The area formerly known as "County Dublin" is now defined in legislation solely as the "Dublin Region" under the <i>Local Government Act, 1991 (Regional Authorities) (Establishment) Order, 1993</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-r1_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and this is the terminology officially used by the four Dublin administrative councils in press releases concerning the former county area. The term <i><a href="/wiki/Greater_Dublin_Area" title="Greater Dublin Area">Greater Dublin Area</a></i>, which might consist of some or all of the Dublin Region along with counties of <a href="/wiki/County_Kildare" title="County Kildare">Kildare</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Meath" title="County Meath">Meath</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_Wicklow" title="County Wicklow">Wicklow</a>, has no legal standing.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dublin_Region">Dublin Region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Dublin Region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <b>Dublin Region</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">NUTS</a> Level III <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="List of regions of the Republic of Ireland">region</a> of Ireland. The region is one of eight regions of the Republic of Ireland for the purposes of <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> statistics. Its NUTS code is IE061.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> It is co-extensive with the old county. The regional capital is <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin City</a> which is also the national capital.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishRegionOffice_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishRegionOffice-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The latest <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Survey_Ireland" title="Ordnance Survey Ireland">Ordnance Survey Ireland</a> "Discovery Series" (Third Edition 2005) 1:50,000 map of the Dublin Region, Sheet 50, shows the boundaries of the city and three surrounding counties of the region. Extremities of the Dublin Region, in the north and south of the region, appear in other sheets of the series, 43 and 56 respectively.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_subdivisions_of_County_Dublin" title="List of subdivisions of County Dublin">List of subdivisions of County Dublin</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dublin_postal_districts" title="List of Dublin postal districts">List of Dublin postal districts</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baronies">Baronies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Baronies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IrelandBaronies1899Map_(Dublin_cropped).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/IrelandBaronies1899Map_%28Dublin_cropped%29.png/190px-IrelandBaronies1899Map_%28Dublin_cropped%29.png" decoding="async" width="190" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/IrelandBaronies1899Map_%28Dublin_cropped%29.png/285px-IrelandBaronies1899Map_%28Dublin_cropped%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/IrelandBaronies1899Map_%28Dublin_cropped%29.png 2x" data-file-width="311" data-file-height="419" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IrelandBaronies1899Map_(Dublin_cropped).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Baronies of County Dublin</div></div></div>\n<p>There are nine historic <a href="/wiki/Barony_(Ireland)" title="Barony (Ireland)">baronies</a> in the county.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> While baronies continue to be officially defined units, they are no longer used for many administrative purposes. The last boundary change of a barony in Dublin was in 1842, when the barony of Balrothery was divided into Balrothery East and Balrothery West. Their official status is illustrated by Placenames Orders made since 2003, where official Irish names of baronies are listed under "Administrative units". The largest barony in Dublin is Uppercross, at 37,307 acres (151 km2), and the smallest barony is Dublin, at 1,693 acres (6.9 km2).\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_baronies_of_Ireland" title="List of baronies of Ireland">List of baronies of Ireland</a></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Balrothery_East" title="Balrothery East">Balrothery East</a> (<i>Baile an Ridire Thoir</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Balrothery_West" title="Balrothery West">Balrothery West</a> (<i>Baile an Ridire Thiar</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Castleknock_(barony)" title="Castleknock (barony)">Castleknock</a> (<i>Caisle\xc3\xa1n Cnucha</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coolock_(barony)" title="Coolock (barony)">Coolock</a> (<i>An Ch\xc3\xbal\xc3\xb3g</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dublin_(barony)" title="Dublin (barony)">Dublin</a> (<i>Baile \xc3\x81tha Cliath</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin City</a> (<i>Cathair Baile \xc3\x81tha Cliath</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nethercross" title="Nethercross">Nethercross</a> (<i>An Chrois \xc3\x8dochtarach</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Newcastle_(County_Dublin_barony)" title="Newcastle (County Dublin barony)">Newcastle</a> (<i>An Caisle\xc3\xa1n Nua</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rathdown_(County_Dublin_barony)" title="Rathdown (County Dublin barony)">Rathdown</a> (<i>R\xc3\xa1th an D\xc3\xbain</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uppercross&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Uppercross (page does not exist)">Uppercross</a> (<i>An Chrois Uachtarach</i>)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Townlands">Townlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Townlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_townlands_of_County_Dublin" title="List of townlands of County Dublin">List of townlands of County Dublin</a></div>\n<p>Townlands are the smallest officially defined geographical divisions in Ireland. There are 1,090 townlands in Dublin, of which 88 are historic town boundaries. These town boundaries are registered as their own townlands and are much larger than rural townlands. The smallest rural townlands in Dublin are just 1 acre in size, most of which are offshore islands (<i>Clare Rock Island, Lamb Island, Maiden Rock, Muglins, Thulla Island</i>). The largest rural townland in Dublin is 2,797 acres (<i>Caastlekelly</i>). The average size of a townland in the county (excluding towns) is 205 acres.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_and_hills_of_County_Dublin" title="List of mountains and hills of County Dublin">List of mountains and hills of County Dublin</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_County_Dublin" title="List of rivers of County Dublin">List of rivers of County Dublin</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:229px;max-width:229px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:227px;max-width:227px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolphin_at_Dalkey_Island_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Dolphin_at_Dalkey_Island_%28cropped%29.jpg/450px-Dolphin_at_Dalkey_Island_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="782" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:227px;max-width:227px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Deer_in_Phoenix_Park,_Dublin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Deer_in_Phoenix_Park%2C_Dublin.jpg/225px-Deer_in_Phoenix_Park%2C_Dublin.jpg" decoding="async" width="225" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Deer_in_Phoenix_Park%2C_Dublin.jpg/338px-Deer_in_Phoenix_Park%2C_Dublin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Deer_in_Phoenix_Park%2C_Dublin.jpg/450px-Deer_in_Phoenix_Park%2C_Dublin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">A <a href="/wiki/Common_bottlenose_dolphin" title="Common bottlenose dolphin">Bottlenose Dolphin</a> (<i>Tursiops truncatus</i>) at <a href="/wiki/Dalkey_Island" title="Dalkey Island">Dalkey Island</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Red_Deer" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Deer">Red Deer</a> (<i>Cervus elaphus</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Park" title="Phoenix Park">Phoenix Park</a></div></div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skerries_Sunset.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Skerries_Sunset.jpg/225px-Skerries_Sunset.jpg" decoding="async" width="225" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Skerries_Sunset.jpg/338px-Skerries_Sunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Skerries_Sunset.jpg/450px-Skerries_Sunset.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skerries_Sunset.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sunset over <a href="/wiki/Skerries,_Dublin" title="Skerries, Dublin">Skerries</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Dublin is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Irish_counties_by_area" title="List of Irish counties by area">third smallest</a> of Ireland\'s 32 counties by area, and the largest in terms of population. It is the third-smallest of Leinster\'s 12 counties in size and the largest by population. Dublin shares a border with three counties - <a href="/wiki/County_Meath" title="County Meath">Meath</a> to the north and west, <a href="/wiki/County_Kildare" title="County Kildare">Kildare</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/County_Wicklow" title="County Wicklow">Wicklow</a> to the south. To the east, Dublin has an <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a> coastline which stretches for roughly 100 kilometres (62&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dublin is a topographically varied region. The city centre is generally very low-lying, and many areas of coastal Dublin are at or near sea-level. In the south of the county, the topography rises steeply from sea-level at the coast to over 500 metres (1,600&#160;ft) in just a few kilometres. This natural barrier has resulted in densely populated coastal settlements in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire%E2%80%93Rathdown" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown</a> and westward urban sprawl in <a href="/wiki/South_Dublin" title="South Dublin">South Dublin</a>. In contrast, <a href="/wiki/Fingal" title="Fingal">Fingal</a> is generally rural in nature and much less densely populated than the rest of the county. Consequently, Fingal is significantly larger than the other three local authorities and covers about 49.5% of County Dublin\'s land area. Fingal is also perhaps the flattest region in Ireland, with the low-lying <a href="/wiki/Naul_Hills" title="Naul Hills">Naul Hills</a> rising to a maximum height of just 176 metres (577&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Dublin is bounded to the south by the <a href="/wiki/Wicklow_Mountains" title="Wicklow Mountains">Wicklow Mountains</a>. Where the mountains extend into County Dublin, they are known locally as the Dublin Mountains (Sl\xc3\xa9ibhte Bhaile \xc3\x81tha Cliath). <a href="/wiki/Kippure" title="Kippure">Kippure</a>, on the Dublin-Wicklow border, is the county\'s highest mountain, at 757 metres (2,484&#160;ft) above sea level. The mountains are a popular amenity area, with <a href="/wiki/Two_Rock" title="Two Rock">Two Rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Three_Rock" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Rock">Three Rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibradden" class="mw-redirect" title="Tibradden">Tibradden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montpelier_Hill" title="Montpelier Hill">Montpelier Hill</a> being among the most heavily foot-falled hiking destinations in Ireland. Forest cover extends to over 6,000 hectares (15,000 acres) within the county, nearly all of which is located in the Dublin Mountains. With just 6.5% of Dublin under forest, it is the 6th least forested county in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Much of the county is drained by the <a href="/wiki/River_Liffey" title="River Liffey">River Liffey</a> and two of its main tributaries, the <a href="/wiki/River_Tolka" title="River Tolka">River Tolka</a> in north Dublin and the <a href="/wiki/River_Dodder" title="River Dodder">River Dodder</a> in south Dublin. The Liffey, at 125 kilometres (78&#160;mi) in length, is the 8th longest river in Ireland, and rises near <a href="/wiki/Tonduff" title="Tonduff">Tonduff</a> in County Wicklow, reaching the Irish Sea at the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Docklands" title="Dublin Docklands">Dublin Docklands</a>. The Liffey cuts through the centre of Dublin city, and the resultant <a href="/wiki/Northside,_Dublin" title="Northside, Dublin">Northside</a>-<a href="/wiki/Southside,_Dublin" title="Southside, Dublin">Southside</a> divide is an often used social, economic and linguistic distinction. In terms of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, the estuarine and coastal areas of the county are home to a wealth ecologically important areas. County Dublin contains 11 <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>-designated <a href="/wiki/Special_Area_of_Conservation" title="Special Area of Conservation">Special Areas of Conservation</a> (SACs) and 11 <a href="/wiki/Special_Protection_Area" title="Special Protection Area">Special Protection Areas</a> (SPAs).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The bedrock geology of Dublin consists primarily of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Carboniferous" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower Carboniferous">Lower Carboniferous</a> limestone, which underlies about two thirds of the entire county, stretching from Skerries to <a href="/wiki/Booterstown" title="Booterstown">Booterstown</a>. During the Lower Carboniferous (ca. 340 Mya), the area was part of a warm tropical sea inhabited by an abundance of <a href="/wiki/Corals" class="mw-redirect" title="Corals">corals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crinoids" class="mw-redirect" title="Crinoids">crinoids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brachiopods" class="mw-redirect" title="Brachiopods">brachiopods</a>. The oldest rocks in Dublin are the <a href="/wiki/Cambrian" title="Cambrian">Cambrian</a> shales located on Howth Head, which were laid down ca. 500 Mya. Disruption following the closure of the <a href="/wiki/Iapetus_Ocean" title="Iapetus Ocean">Iapetus Ocean</a> approximately 400 <a href="/wiki/Geologic_time_scale" title="Geologic time scale">Mya</a> resulted in the formation of <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> This is now exposed at the surface from the Dublin Mountains to the coastal areas of D\xc3\xban Laoghaire. 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">Lead</a> extraction and smelting at the <a href="/wiki/Ballycorus_Leadmines" title="Ballycorus Leadmines">Ballycorus Leadmines</a> caused widespread <a href="/wiki/Lead_poisoning" title="Lead poisoning">lead poisoning</a>, and the area was once nicknamed "Death Valley".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prominent_geographic_features">Prominent geographic features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Prominent geographic features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dublin_Bay" title="Dublin Bay">Dublin Bay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dublin_Mountains_Way" title="Dublin Mountains Way">Dublin Mountains</a></li>\n<li>Glenasmole Valley</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Howth_Head" title="Howth Head">Howth Head</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Killiney_Hill" title="Killiney Hill">Killiney Hill</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Montpelier_Hill" title="Montpelier Hill">Montpelier Hill</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Park" title="Phoenix Park">Phoenix Park</a></li>\n<li>Rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Liffey" title="River Liffey">Liffey</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Dodder" title="River Dodder">Dodder</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Tolka" title="River Tolka">Tolka</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rogerstown_Estuary" title="Rogerstown Estuary">Rogerstown Estuary</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ticknock" title="Ticknock">Ticknock Forest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Portmarnock" title="Portmarnock">Velvet Strand</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IMG_Kippure0232w.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/IMG_Kippure0232w.jpg/220px-IMG_Kippure0232w.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IMG_Kippure0232w.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>At an elevation of 757 metres (2,484 ft), <a href="/wiki/Kippure" title="Kippure">Kippure</a> is the highest point in the county</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandycove,_Summer_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" title="Sandycove">Sandycove</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Snow_in_Killiney,_Dublin_(2010).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Snow_in_Killiney%2C_Dublin_%282010%29.jpg/220px-Snow_in_Killiney%2C_Dublin_%282010%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Snow_in_Killiney%2C_Dublin_%282010%29.jpg/330px-Snow_in_Killiney%2C_Dublin_%282010%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Snow_in_Killiney%2C_Dublin_%282010%29.jpg/440px-Snow_in_Killiney%2C_Dublin_%282010%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Snow_in_Killiney,_Dublin_(2010).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>December snow at <a href="/wiki/Killiney" title="Killiney">Killiney</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Dublin is in a maritime <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic</a> region according to <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a>. Its climate is characterised by cool winters, mild humid summers, and a lack of temperature extremes. <a href="/wiki/Met_%C3%89ireann" title="Met \xc3\x89ireann">Met \xc3\x89ireann</a> have a number of weather stations in the county, with its two primary stations at <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Casement_Aerodrome" title="Casement Aerodrome">Casement Aerodrome</a>.\n</p><p>Annual temperatures typically fall within a narrow range. In <a href="/wiki/Merrion_Square" title="Merrion Square">Merrion Square</a>, the coldest month is February, with an average minimum temperature of 2.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C (36.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and the hottest month is July, with an average maximum temperature of 20.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Due to the <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">urban heat island</a> effect, Dublin city has the warmest summertime nights in Ireland. The average minimum temperature at Merrion Square in July is 13.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (56.3&#160;\xc2\xb0F), similar to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> At Dublin Airport, the driest month is February with 48.8&#160;mm (2&#160;in) of rainfall, and the wettest month is November, with 79.0&#160;mm (3&#160;in) of rain on average.\n</p><p>As the prevailing wind direction in Ireland is from the south and west, the Wicklow Mountains create a <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> over much of the county. Dublin\'s sheltered location makes it the driest place in Ireland, receiving only about half the rainfall of the west coast. <a href="/wiki/Ringsend" title="Ringsend">Ringsend</a> in the south of Dublin city records the lowest rainfall in the country, with an average annual precipitation of 683&#160;mm (27&#160;in). The wettest area of the county is the Glenasmole Valley, which receives 1,159&#160;mm (46&#160;in) of rainfall per year. As a temperate coastal county, snow is relatively uncommon in lowland areas; however, Dublin is particularly vulnerable to heavy snowfall on rare occasions where cold, dry easterly winds dominate during the winter.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>During the late summer and early autumn, Dublin can experience Atlantic storms, which bring strong winds and torrential rain to Ireland. Dublin was the county worst-affected by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charley_(1986)" title="Hurricane Charley (1986)">Hurricane Charley</a> in 1986. It caused severe flooding, especially along the River Dodder, and is reputed to be the worst flood event in Dublin\'s history. Rainfall records were shattered across the county. Kippure recorded 280&#160;mm (11&#160;in) of rain over a 24-hour period, the greatest daily rainfall total ever recorded in Ireland. The government allocated <a href="/wiki/Irish_pound" title="Irish pound">IR\xc2\xa3</a>6,449,000 (equivalent to US$20.5 million in 2020) to repair the damage wrought by Charley.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The two reservoirs at Bohernabreena in the Dublin Mountains were upgraded in 2006 after a study into the impact of Hurricane Charley concluded that a slightly larger storm would have caused the reservoir dams to burst, which would have resulted in catastrophic damage and significant loss of life.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Offshore_Islands">Offshore Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Offshore Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In contrast with the <a href="/wiki/Wild_Atlantic_Way" title="Wild Atlantic Way">Atlantic Coast</a>, the east coast of Ireland has relatively few islands. County Dublin has the highest concentration of islands on the Irish east coast. Colt Island, St. Patrick\'s Island and Shenick Island are clustered off the coast of Skerries, and are collectively known as the "Skerries Islands Natural Heritage Area". Further out lies <a href="/wiki/Rockabill" title="Rockabill">Rockabill</a>, which is Dublin\'s most isolated island, at about 6 kilometres (3.7&#160;mi) offshore. <a href="/wiki/Lambay_Island" title="Lambay Island">Lambay Island</a>, at 250 hectares (620 acres), is the largest island off Ireland\'s east coast and the easternmost point of County Dublin. Lambay supports one of the largest seabird colonies in Ireland and, curiously, also supports a population of non-native <a href="/wiki/Red-necked_wallaby" title="Red-necked wallaby">Red-necked wallabies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Alt_126m_MV_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alt_126m_MV-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  To the south of Lambay lies a smaller island known as <a href="/wiki/Ireland%27s_Eye" title="Ireland&#39;s Eye">Ireland\'s Eye</a> - the result of a mistranslation of the island\'s Irish name by invading <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a>. \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bull_Island" title="Bull Island">Bull Island</a> is a man-made island lying roughly parallel to the shoreline which began to form following the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Bull_Wall" title="Bull Wall">Bull Wall</a> in 1825. The island is still growing and is currently 5 kilometres (3.1&#160;mi) long and 0.8 kilometres (0.50&#160;mi) wide. In 1981, North Bull Island (<i>Oile\xc3\xa1n an Tairbh Thuaidh</i>) was designated as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> biosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1021810730">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cityscape_At_Sunset_Dublin_Ireland_Cityscape_Photography_(179394129).jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> is the largest city in Ireland</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:County_Dublin_Population_Density_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/County_Dublin_Population_Density_Map.png/230px-County_Dublin_Population_Density_Map.png" decoding="async" width="230" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/County_Dublin_Population_Density_Map.png/345px-County_Dublin_Population_Density_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/County_Dublin_Population_Density_Map.png/460px-County_Dublin_Population_Density_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="2584" data-file-height="2480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:County_Dublin_Population_Density_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population density map of County Dublin</div></div></div>\n<p>As of the 2016 Census, the population of Dublin was 1,345,402, a 5.7% increase since the <a href="/wiki/Census_of_Ireland_2011" title="Census of Ireland 2011">2011 Census</a>. The county\'s population first surpassed 1&#160;million in 1981, and is projected to reach between 1.5&#160;million and 1.7&#160;million by 2031.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dublin is Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_Irish_counties_by_population" title="List of Irish counties by population">most populous county</a>, a position it has held since the 1901 Census, when it overtook <a href="/wiki/County_Cork" title="County Cork">County Cork</a>. As of 2016, Dublin has over twice the population of <a href="/wiki/County_Antrim" title="County Antrim">Antrim</a> and two and a half times the population of Cork. Approximately 20.5% of Ireland\'s population lives within County Dublin (27% if only the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> is counted). Additionally, Dublin has more people than the combined populations of Ireland\'s 16 smallest counties.\n</p><p>With an area of just 922&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (356&#160;sq&#160;mi), Dublin is by far the most densely populated county in Ireland. The population density of the county is 1,459 people per square kilometre - nearly 7 times higher than Ireland\'s second most densely populated county, <a href="/wiki/County_Down" title="County Down">County Down</a> in Northern Ireland.\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Tiger" title="Celtic Tiger">Celtic Tiger</a> period, a large number of Dublin natives (<i><a href="/wiki/Dubliners" title="Dubliners">Dubliners</a></i>) moved to the rapidly expanding commuter towns in the adjoining counties. As of 2016, approximately 25.8% (305,996) of Dubliners were living outside of County Dublin. People born within Dublin comprise 28% of the population of <a href="/wiki/County_Meath" title="County Meath">Meath</a>, 31% of <a href="/wiki/County_Kildare" title="County Kildare">Kildare</a> and 35% of <a href="/wiki/County_Wicklow" title="County Wicklow">Wicklow</a>. There are 880,457 Dublin natives living within the county, accounting for 66.8% of the population. People born in other Irish counties living within Dublin account for roughly 12.4% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 2011 and 2016, international migration produced a net increase of 25,261 people. Dublin has the highest proportion of international residents of any county in Ireland, with around 21% of the county\'s population being born outside of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of the 2016 Census, 6.8 percent of the county\'s population was reported as younger than 5 years old, 25.2 percent were between 5 and 25, 55.8 percent were between 25 and 65, and 12.2 percent of the population was older than 65. Of this latter group, 18,276 people (1.4 percent) were over the age of 80. The population was evenly split between females (50.14 percent) and males (49.86 percent).\n</p><p>In 2019, there were 17,682 births within the county, and the average age of a first time mother was 31.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="float:right;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td colspan="2"><b>Main immigrant groups, 2016</b><sup id="cite_ref-41" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, SAR</a></i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Just over one fifth (20.8 percent) of County Dublin\'s population was born outside of the Republic of Ireland. In 2016, Fingal had the highest percentage of non-nationals in Dublin (23.2 percent), and South Dublin had the lowest (17.5 percent). The immigrant population of Dublin is mainly from other European countries, however there are also substantial numbers of <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilians" title="Brazilians">Brazilians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Americans" title="Americans">Americans</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Asians" class="mw-redirect" title="East Asians">East Asians</a> living in the county. Immigrants from other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states comprise 10.4 percent of Dublin\'s population, and those from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> a further 5.3 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest sources of foreign-born residents in Dublin are the United Kingdom and Poland, although the growth of these two groups has slowed in recent years. Prior to the 2000s, the UK was historically the largest single source of non-nationals living in Dublin. Of those born in the UK, 76.3 percent were born in <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Britain</a>, and the remaining 23.7 percent were born in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. Between 2011 and 2016, the number of UK-born residents living in Dublin declined by 1.8 percent. \n</p><p>There is a large difference between the number of people living in Dublin who were born in the UK (55,391) and those who stated that they were UK citizens in the 2016 census (19,196). This discrepancy can arise for a variety of factors, such as people born in Northern Ireland claiming <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationality_law" title="Irish nationality law">Irish citizenship</a> rather than UK citizenship, Irish people born in the UK who now live in Dublin, British people who have become <a href="/wiki/Naturalization" title="Naturalization">natural</a> citizens, and foreign residents of Dublin who were born in the UK but are not UK citizens. Depending on an individual\'s responses in the census, all of these examples could result in the country of birth being registered by the CSO as the United Kingdom, but nationality being registered as Irish or a third country.\n</p><p>Following its <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">accession to the EU</a>, the Polish quickly became the fastest growing immigrant community in Dublin. Just 188 Poles had applied for Irish work permits in 1999. By 2006 this number had grown to 93,787.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Post-2008_Irish_economic_downturn" title="Post-2008 Irish economic downturn">2008 Irish economic downturn</a>, as many as 3,000 Poles left Ireland each month. Despite this, Poles still account for roughly one quarter of Dublin\'s EU foreign residents, and are the largest non-national group in the county, as well as the second largest foreign-born group.\n</p><p>As of 2016, the fastest growing major immigrant group in Dublin was Romanians. Despite being an EU member since 2007, Ireland had restrictions on the number of Romanians who could emigrate to the country until 2012. The removal of the restrictions was followed by a significant increase in the number of Romanians living in Dublin. The five year period from 2011 to 2016 saw a 67.7 percent increase in the number of Romanians living in Dublin, who are now the county\'s third largest foreign national group. County Dublin is home to around 58 percent of Ireland\'s Romanian community. \n</p><p>Outside of Europe, Brazil and India are the largest and fastest growing sources of foreign residents in Dublin. The number of Brazilians living in Dublin increased by 48.5 percent between 2011 and 2016, primarily driven by Ireland\'s participation in the Brazilian government\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Ci%C3%AAncia_sem_Fronteiras" title="Ci\xc3\xaancia sem Fronteiras">Ci\xc3\xaancia sem Fronteiras</a></i> programme, which sees thousands of Brazilian students come to study in Ireland each year, many of whom remain in the country afterwards. Dublin\'s Indian community grew by 15.1 percent from 2011-2016, and Indians are now the fourth largest migrant group in the county. The influx of Indians is primarily driven by multinational tech companies such as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> who have located their European headquarters within the county, in areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Docks" title="Silicon Docks">Silicon Docks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandyford" title="Sandyford">Sandyford</a>. In August 2020, the first dedicated Hindu temple in Ireland was built in <a href="/wiki/Walkinstown" title="Walkinstown">Walkinstown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the Central Statistics Office, in 2016 the population of County Dublin self-identified as:\n</p>\n<ul><li>87.6% White (75.5% White Irish, 11.7% Other White Background, 0.5% Irish Traveler)</li>\n<li>3.8% <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a></li>\n<li>2.3% Mixed background</li>\n<li>2.2% Black</li>\n<li>4.1% Not Stated</li></ul>\n<p>By ethnicity, in 2016 the population was 87.6% white. Those who identified as White Irish constituted 75.5% of the county\'s population, and <a href="/wiki/Irish_Traveler" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Traveler">Irish Travelers</a> comprised a further 0.5%. Caucasians who did not identify as ethnically Irish accounted for 11.7% of the population.  \n</p><p>In terms of total numbers, Dublin has the largest non-white population Ireland, with an estimated 109,732 residents, accounting for 8.3% of the county\'s population. Nearly half (44.7 percent) of Ireland\'s black residents live within the county. In terms of percentage of population, Fingal has the highest percentage of both black (3.9 percent) and non-white (10.1 percent) residents of any local authority in Ireland. Conversely, D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown in the south of the county has one of Ireland\'s lowest percentages of black residents, with only 0.67% of the population identifying as black in 2016. Additionally, 42.8% of Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Multiracial_people" title="Multiracial people">multiracial</a> population lives within County Dublin.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Dublin (2016)</th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">religion</td>\n<td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">percent</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:purple; width:68.9%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">68.9%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">No religion</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:black; width:14.4%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">14.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Other Christian</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:dodgerblue; width:7.0%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">7.0%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:green; width:2.2%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:red; width:0.6%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other stated religions</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:yellow; width:2.9%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2.9%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Not Stated</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:grey; width:4.1%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">4.1%</td>\n</tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral,_Dublin_(40282975540).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral%2C_Dublin_%2840282975540%29.jpg/220px-St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral%2C_Dublin_%2840282975540%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral%2C_Dublin_%2840282975540%29.jpg/330px-St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral%2C_Dublin_%2840282975540%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral%2C_Dublin_%2840282975540%29.jpg/440px-St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral%2C_Dublin_%2840282975540%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral,_Dublin_(40282975540).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral,_Dublin" title="St Patrick&#39;s Cathedral, Dublin">St Patrick\'s Cathedral</a>, founded in 1191</div></div></div>\n<p>The largest <a href="/wiki/Religious_denomination" title="Religious denomination">religious denomination</a> by both number of adherents and as a percentage of Dublin\'s population in 2016 was the Roman Catholic Church, with 68.9 percent. All other Christian denominations including <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian">Presbyterian</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> accounted for 7.0 percent of Dublin\'s population. Together, all denominations of Christianity accounted for 75.9 percent of the county\'s population. According to the 2016 census, Dublin city is the least religious local authority in Ireland, with 18.1 percent of the population declaring themselves non-religious, followed closely by D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown and <a href="/wiki/Galway_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Galway city">Galway city</a> (17.1 percent). In the county as a whole, those unaffiliated with any religion represented 14.4 percent of the population, which is the largest percentage of non-religious people of any county in Ireland.\n</p><p>Of the non-Christian religions, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the largest in terms of number of adherents, with Muslims accounting for 2.2% of the population. After Islam, the largest non-Christian religions in 2016 were <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (0.62 percent), <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (0.32 percent) and <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> (0.11 percent). While small in percentage terms, County Dublin contains over half of Ireland\'s Hindu (58.4 percent), Jewish (56.3 percent) and Eastern Orthodox (52.1%) residents, and just under half of its Islamic (47.3 percent) and Buddhist (44.0 percent) residents.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Dublin and its hinterland has been a Christian <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Dublin" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Dublin">diocese</a> since 1028. For centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Primacy_of_Ireland" title="Primacy of Ireland">Primacy of Ireland</a> was disputed between Dublin, the social and political capital of Ireland, and <a href="/wiki/Armagh" title="Armagh">Armagh</a>, site of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick" title="Saint Patrick">Saint Patrick</a>\'s main church, which was founded in 445 AD. In 1353 the dispute was settled by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_VI" title="Pope Innocent VI">Pope Innocent VI</a>, who proclaimed that the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Dublin" title="Archbishop of Dublin">Archbishop of Dublin</a> was <i>Primate of Ireland</i>, while the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Armagh" title="Archbishop of Armagh">Archbishop of Armagh</a> was titled <i>Primate of All Ireland</i>. These two distinct titles were replicated in the Church of Ireland following the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a>. Historically, County Dublin was the epicentre of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Ireland" title="Protestantism in Ireland">Protestantism in Ireland</a> outside of <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a>. Records from the <a href="/wiki/1891_United_Kingdom_census" title="1891 United Kingdom census">1891 census</a> show that the county was 21.4 percent Protestant towards the end of the 19th century. By the 1911 census this had gradually declined to around 20% due to poor economic conditions, as Dublin Protestants moved to industrial <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">War of Independence</a> (1919-1921), Dublin\'s Protestant community went into a steady decline, falling to 8.5 percent of the population by 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Between the 2011 and 2016 census, the fastest growing religions in Dublin were <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelicalism</a> (111.7 percent), Eastern Orthodox (41.0 percent), Hinduism (30.1 percent) and Islam (17.7 percent), while the most rapidly declining religions were <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist</a>/<a href="/wiki/Wesleyan_theology" title="Wesleyan theology">Wesleyan</a> (-9.6 percent), Catholicism (-5.5 percent) and <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a> (-4.7 percent).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_Area">Metropolitan Area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Metropolitan Area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dublin_city">Dublin city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Dublin city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The boundaries of <a href="/wiki/Dublin_City_Council" title="Dublin City Council">Dublin City Council</a> comprise the urban core of the city, often referred to as <i>"Dublin city centre"</i>, an area of 117.8 square kilometres. This encompasses the central suburbs of the city, extending as far south as <a href="/wiki/Terenure" title="Terenure">Terenure</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donnybrook,_Dublin" title="Donnybrook, Dublin">Donnybrook</a>; as far north as <a href="/wiki/Ballymun" title="Ballymun">Ballymun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donaghmede" title="Donaghmede">Donaghmede</a>; and as far west as <a href="/wiki/Ballyfermot" title="Ballyfermot">Ballyfermot</a>. As of 2016, there were 554,554 people living within Dublin city centre. However, as the continuous <a href="/wiki/Built-up_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Built-up area">built-up area</a> extends beyond the city boundaries, the term <i>"Dublin city and suburbs"</i> is commonly employed when referring to the actual extent of Dublin.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_City_Boundaries_2020.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Dublin_City_Boundaries_2020.png/230px-Dublin_City_Boundaries_2020.png" decoding="async" width="230" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Dublin_City_Boundaries_2020.png/345px-Dublin_City_Boundaries_2020.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Dublin_City_Boundaries_2020.png/460px-Dublin_City_Boundaries_2020.png 2x" data-file-width="2552" data-file-height="2480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_City_Boundaries_2020.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Greater Dublin\'s defined boundaries</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dublin_city_and_suburbs">Dublin city and suburbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Dublin city and suburbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Dublin city and suburbs is a CSO-designated urban area which includes the densely populated contiguous built-up area which surrounds Dublin city centre. It encompasses 317.5 square kilometres and contains approximately 87% of County Dublin\'s population (1,173,179 people) as of the 2016 census.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dublin_Metropolitan_Area">Dublin Metropolitan Area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Dublin Metropolitan Area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As the <a href="/wiki/City_proper" title="City proper">city proper</a> does not extend beyond <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin Airport</a>, the towns of "North County Dublin" such as Swords, Lusk, Rush and Malahide are not considered part of the city, and are recorded by the CSO as separate settlements. Under Ireland\'s National Planning Framework, these towns are considered part of the Dublin Metropolitan Area (DMA). The DMA also includes towns outside of the county, such as <a href="/wiki/Naas" title="Naas">Naas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leixlip" title="Leixlip">Leixlip</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maynooth" title="Maynooth">Maynooth</a> in County Kildare, and <a href="/wiki/Bray,_County_Wicklow" title="Bray, County Wicklow">Bray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greystones" title="Greystones">Greystones</a> in County Wicklow, but does not include Balbriggan or Skerries, which are located in the far north of County Dublin.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greater_Dublin_Area">Greater Dublin Area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Greater Dublin Area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Dublin_Area" title="Greater Dublin Area">Greater Dublin Area</a> (GDA) is a commonly used planning jurisdiction which extends to the wider network of commuter towns that are economically connected to Dublin city. The GDA consists of County Dublin and its three neighboring counties, Meath, Kildare and Wicklow. With a population of 1.9 million and an area of 6,986 square kilometres, it contains 40% of the population of the State, and covers 9.9% of its land area. \n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire-Rathdown" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire-Rathdown">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire-Rathdown</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Meath" title="County Meath">Meath</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Kildare" title="County Kildare">Kildare</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Wicklow" title="County Wicklow">Wicklow</a>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_Areas">Urban Areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Urban Areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Central_Statistics_Office_(Ireland)" title="Central Statistics Office (Ireland)">CSO</a> classification, an "Urban Area" is a town with a population greater than 1,500. Dublin is the most urbanised county in Ireland, with 97.75% of its residents residing in urban areas as of 2016. Of Dublin\'s three non-city local authorities, Fingal has the highest proportion of people living in rural areas (7.9%), while D\xc3\xban Laoghaire-Rathdown has the lowest (1.19%). The western suburbs of Dublin city such as <a href="/wiki/Tallaght" title="Tallaght">Tallaght</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blanchardstown" title="Blanchardstown">Blanchardstown</a> have experienced rapid growth in recent decades, and both areas have a population roughly equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Galway_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Galway city">Galway city</a>. \n</p>\n<table class="navbox">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title"><div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div><style href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KILLINEY-147_(1424762996).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/KILLINEY-147_%281424762996%29.jpg/240px-KILLINEY-147_%281424762996%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/KILLINEY-147_%281424762996%29.jpg/360px-KILLINEY-147_%281424762996%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/KILLINEY-147_%281424762996%29.jpg/480px-KILLINEY-147_%281424762996%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="976" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KILLINEY-147_(1424762996).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of Killiney Bay from <a href="/wiki/Killiney_Hill" title="Killiney Hill">Killiney Hill</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Local radio stations include <a href="/wiki/Dublin%27s_98FM" title="Dublin&#39;s 98FM">98FM</a>, <a href="/wiki/FM104" title="FM104">FM104</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_City_FM" title="Dublin City FM">Dublin City FM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin%27s_Q102" title="Dublin&#39;s Q102">Q102</a>, <a href="/wiki/SPIN_1038" title="SPIN 1038">SPIN 1038</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_106.8" title="Sunshine 106.8">Sunshine 106.8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Na_Life" title="Raidi\xc3\xb3 Na Life">Raidi\xc3\xb3 Na Life</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radio_Nova_100FM_(Ireland)" title="Radio Nova 100FM (Ireland)">Radio Nova</a>.\n</p><p>Local newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Echo_(Dublin_newspaper)" title="The Echo (Dublin newspaper)">The Echo</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Liffey_Champion" title="Liffey Champion">Liffey Champion</a></i>.\n</p><p>Most of the area can receive the five main UK television channels as well as the main Irish channels, along with Sky TV and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media_Ireland" title="Virgin Media Ireland">Virgin Media Ireland</a> cable television.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><b>Road:</b> The major roads are the  <a href="/wiki/N2_road_(Ireland)" title="N2 road (Ireland)">N2</a>, <a href="/wiki/N3_road_(Ireland)" title="N3 road (Ireland)">N3</a>, <a href="/wiki/N4_road_(Ireland)" title="N4 road (Ireland)">N4</a> and <a href="/wiki/N7_road_(Ireland)" title="N7 road (Ireland)">N7</a> national primary roads, and the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway_(Republic_of_Ireland)" title="M1 motorway (Republic of Ireland)">M1</a>, <a href="/wiki/N11_road_(Ireland)" title="N11 road (Ireland)">M11</a> and <a href="/wiki/M50_motorway_(Ireland)" title="M50 motorway (Ireland)">M50</a> motorways.</li>\n<li><b>Heavy rail:</b> The <a href="/wiki/InterCity_(Iarnr%C3%B3d_%C3%89ireann)" title="InterCity (Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann)">InterCity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commuter_(Iarnr%C3%B3d_%C3%89ireann)" title="Commuter (Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann)">Commuter</a> rail services (<a href="/wiki/Iarnr%C3%B3d_%C3%89ireann" title="Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann">Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann</a>).</li>\n<li><b>Light rail:</b> The <a href="/wiki/Luas" title="Luas">Luas</a> tram system serving <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin City</a> and its southern and western suburbs.</li>\n<li><b>Rapid transit:</b> The <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Dublin Area Rapid Transit">DART</a></li>\n<li><b>Port:</b> <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Port" title="Dublin Port">Dublin Port</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire Harbour</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Air:</b> <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin Airport</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The economy of County Dublin was identified as being the powerhouse behind the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Tiger" title="Celtic Tiger">Celtic Tiger</a>, a period of strong economic growth of the state. This resulted in the economy of the county expanding by almost 100% between the early 1990s and 2007. This growth resulted from incoming high-value industries, such as financial services and <a href="/wiki/Software_manufacturing" title="Software manufacturing">software manufacturing</a>, as well as low-skilled retail and domestic services, which caused a shift away from older manufacturing industry.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishRegionOffice_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishRegionOffice-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> This change saw high unemployment in the 1980s and early 1990s which resulted in damage to the capital\'s social structure.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishRegionOffice_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishRegionOffice-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to CSO figures, the region had a GDP of \xe2\x82\xac87.238 bn and a GDP per capita of \xe2\x82\xac68,208 in 2014 (the second highest was Cork at \xe2\x82\xac50,544 per capita).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Separately, Eurostat figures for 2012 suggested the region then had a GDP of \xe2\x82\xac72.384 bn and a GDP per capita of \xe2\x82\xac57,200 \xe2\x80\x93 the highest on the island of Ireland (the second highest being Cork with \xe2\x82\xac48,500).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>As of early 2017, the unemployment rate for the Dublin region was estimated at 6%.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_2">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=County_Dublin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Dublin" title="Transport in Dublin">Transport in Dublin</a></div>\n<p>County Dublin is the main transport node of Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-IrishRegionOffice_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishRegionOffice-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and contains one international airport, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin Airport</a>. It is also served by two main seaports, D\xc3\xban Laoghaire port and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Port" title="Dublin Port">Dublin Port</a>, which is just located outside of the city center.  The two main train stations are <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Heuston" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Heuston">Dublin Heuston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Connolly" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Connolly">Dublin Connolly</a>, both of which serve intercity trains.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Towns_and_suburbs">Towns and suburbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
